Conditions of Admission and Consent for Outpatient Care

In this document, "Patient" means the person recetving treatment. "Patient Representative" means any person acting on behalf of the Patient and signing as the Patient’s representative. Use of the word “T,” “you,” “your” or “me” may in context include both the Patient and the Patient Representative. With respect to financial obligations

“T’ or “me” may also, depending on the context, mean financial guarantor “Guarantor”.

"Provider" means the hospital and may include healthcare professionals on the hospital’s staff and/or hospital- based physicians, which include but are not limited to: Emergency Department Physicians, Pathologists, Radiologists, Anesthesiologists, Hospitalists, certain other licensed independent practitioners and any authorized agents, contractors, affiliates, successors or assignees acting on their behalf.

1. Legal Relationship between Hospital and Physicians and Advanced Practice Professionals. I understand and acknowledge that the physicians and advanced practice professionals providing services to me in the hospital are independent contractors and not agents or employees of the hospital. "Advanced Practice Professionals" include, but are not limited to, my treating physicians/ surgeons, radiologists, pathologists, cardiologists, emergency physicians, anesthesiologists, contract physicians, hospital-based physicians, physician assistants, registered nurses, advanced practice registered nurses, certified nurse midwives, certified registered nurse anesthetists, clinical psychologists, clinical nurse specialists, doctors of nursing practice, radiology assistants, and anesthesiology assistants. Independent physicians and Advanced Practice Professionals are responsible for their own actions and the hospital shall not be liable for the acts or omissions of any such independent physicians and/ or Advanced Practice Professionals.

2. Consent to Treatment. I consent to the procedures that may be performed during this hospitalization or during an outpatient episode of care, including, but not limited to, emergency treatment or services, and which may include laboratory procedures, x-ray examination, diagnostic procedures, medical, nursing or surgical treatment or procedures, anesthesia, or hospital services rendered as ordered by the Provider. I consent to allowing residents and other individuals enrolled in a healthcare professional education program as part of their training in health care education to participate in the delivery of my medical care and treatment or be observers while I receive medical care and treatment at the Hospital, and that they will be supervised by instructors and/or hospital staff. I further consent to the hospital conducting blood-borne infectious disease testing, including but not limited to, testing for hepatitis, Acquired Immune Deficiency Syndrome (“AIDS”), and Human Immunodeficiency Virus (“HIV”), if a Provider orders such tests or if ordered by protocol. I understand that the potential side effects and complications of this testing are generally minor and are comparable to the routine collection of blood specimens, including discomfort from the needle stick and/or slight burning, bleeding or soreness at the puncture site. The results of this test will become part of my confidential medical record.

3. Consent to Treatment Using Telemedicine. I consent to treatment involving the use of electronic communications ("Telemedicine") to enable health care providers at different locations to share my individual patient medical information for diagnosis, therapy, follow-up, and/or education purposes. I consent to forwarding my information to a third party as needed to receive Telemedicine services, and I understand that existing confidentiality protections apply. I acknowledge that while Telemedicine can be used to provide improved access to care, as with any medical procedure, there are potential risks and no results can be guaranteed or assured. These risks include, but are not limited to: technical problems with the information transmission or equipment

4. Use of Biological Samples. During your care at the facility, biological samples (such as blood and tissue samples) might be collected from you for purposes of your care. Sometimes, after your visit there might be excess or leftover biological samples no longer needed for your care. These samples are usually discarded. However, sometimes these samples might be used for research within our hospitals and occasionally made available to researchers at external groups such as universities, private companies, advocacy groups, and government agencies. The research can help answer questions about the causes of diseases, how to prevent them, or even how to treat them. Please note that for this kind of research, (i) there might be no practical way to inform you about the details or results of the research (even if it involves genetic research), (i1) generally, no results on tests performed on your samples during the research can be returned to you or entered into your health record, (iii) it is not likely that you will directly benefit from the research, and (iv) there are no plans to compensate or recognize you for use of your samples or any discoveries made during the research. When these samples are used in this manner, your privacy is safeguarded consistent with applicable federal and state privacy laws.

5. Consent to Medication Not Yet FDA Approved and/or Medication Prepared/Repackaged by Outsourcing or Compounding Pharmacy. As part of the services provided, you may be treated with a medication that has not received FDA approval. You may also receive a medication that has been prepared or repackaged by an outsourcing facility or compounding pharmacy. Certain medications for which there are no alternatives or which your physician recommends may be necessary for potentially life-saving treatment.

6. Consent to Product Patient Assistance Programs Limited Power of Attorney (“LPOA"). The Provider may be able to get free replacement or reimbursement for the cost of your drugs or medical products from the companies that make them through a patient assistance program sponsored by the companies that make your drugs or medical products and through charity foundations. If the hospital obtains replacement or reimbursement of cost of your drug or medical product from the manufacturer through such programs, the charge for the product or drug will be removed from your bill. Patient assistance programs require you to sign an application form in order for the hospital to obtain replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted to qualifying patients. This LPOA allows the Provider and its claims processor to complete and sign your patient assistance program applications for you for so long as this program may be available to you.

I hereby appoint hospital and/or its claims processor, my attorney-in-fact for the sole and exclusive purpose of signing patient assistance program application forms on my behalf, so that hospital may attempt to obtain replacement or credits of certain drugs administered or devices implanted from the companies that make them. I understand that the final decision as to my acceptance in a patient assistance program lies with each pharmaceutical or medical device company and that submission by hospital provides no guarantee or assurance that any application will be approved. I will provide reasonable assistance and additional information and documentation as necessary to support each application.

7. Consent to Photographs, and Video, Digital and Audio Recordings. I consent to photographs, video, digital or audio recordings, and/or images of me being recorded for patient care, healthcare operations, security purposes and/or the hospital’s quality improvement and/or risk management activities. I understand that the facility retains the ownership rights to the images and/or recordings. I will be allowed to request access to or copies of the images and/or recordings when technologically feasible unless otherwise prohibited by law. I understand that these images and/or recordings will be securely stored and protected. Images and/or recordings in which I am identified will not be released and/or used outside of the facility without a specific written authorization from me or my legal representative unless otherwise required by law.

8. Financial Agreement. In consideration of the services to be rendered to Patient, Patient or Guarantor individually promises to pay the Patient’s account at the rates stated in the hospital’s price list (known as the "Charge Master" ) effective on the date the charge is processed for the service provided, which rates are hereby expressly incorporated by reference as the price term of this agreement to pay the Patient’s account. Some special items will be priced separately if there is no price listed on the Charge Master. An estimate of the anticipated charges for services to be provided to the Patient is available upon request from the hospital. Estimates may vary significantly from the final charges based on a variety of factors, including, but not limited to, the course of treatment, intensity of care, physician practices, and the necessity of providing additional goods and services.

The hospital will provide a medical screening examination as required to all Patients who are seeking medical services to determine if there is an emergency medical condition without regard to the Patient’s ability to pay. If there is an emergency medical condition, the hospital will provide stabilizing treatment within its capacity. However, Patient and Guarantor understand that if Patient does not qualify under the hospital’s charity care policy or other applicable policy, Patient or Guarantor is not relieved of his/her obligation to pay for these services.

10. Third Party Collection. I acknowledge that the Providers may utilize the services of a third party Business Associate or affiliated entity as an extended business office (“EBO Servicer’’) for medical account billing and servicing. During the time that the medical account is being serviced by the EBO Servicer, the account shall not be considered delinquent, past due or in default. When the EBO Servicer’s efforts to obtain payment have been exhausted due to a number of factors (for e.g., Patient or Guarantor’s failure to pay or make a payment arrangement after insurance adjustments and payments have been credited, and/or the insurer’s denial of claim(s) or benefits is received), the EBO Servicer will send a final notice letter which will include the date that the medical account may be returned from the EBO Servicer to the Provider. Upon return to the Provider by the EBO Servicer, the Provider may place the account back with the EBO Servicer, or, at the option of the Provider, may determine the account to be delinquent, past due and in default.

(Cc) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex. GFR values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative ef Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73 square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation, This formula is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will not calculate if the sex 1s Unknown or if the patient's age is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eGFR along with this new result until December 31, 2022.

(D}) Units of measure: ml/min/1,73 m2

Stages of Kidney Damage according to the National Kidney Foundation are defined as follows:

Stage 1 Kidney damage with normal kidney function >= 90 ml/min/1.73 m2

Stage 2 Kidney damage with mildly decreased kidney function 60-89 ml/min/1.73 m2

Stage 3a Kidney damage with mildly to moderately decreased

kidney function 45-59 ml/min/1.73 m2 Stage 3b Kidney damage with moderately to severely decreased kidney function 30-44 ml/min/1.73 m2 Stage 4 Kidney damage with severely decreased kidney

function 15-29 ml/min/1.73 m2 Stage 5 Kidney failure <15 ml/min/1.73 m2

(I) The Glomerular Filtration Rate is a calculated parameter based on serum Creatinine levels, patient age, and sex, GFR values less than 60 mL/min/1.73 square meters are indicative of Chronic Kidney Disease. Values less than 15 mL/min/1.73 square meters indicate Kidney failure. The calculation for GFR is based on the CKD-EPI(2021) calculation. This formula is race indifferent and is the recommended formula for GFR by the National Kidney Foundation for adults. The GFR will not calculate if the sex is Unknown or if the patient's age is <18 years. We will continue to report a race factor eCFR along with this new result until December 31, 2022,

Important Message from Medicare

Your Rights as a Hospital Inpatient:

* You can receive Medicare covered services. This includes medically necessary hospital services and

services you may need after you are discharged, if ordered by your doctor. You have a right to know about these services, who will pay for them, and where you can get them.

* You can be involved in any decisions about your hospital stay. ; You can report any concerns you have about the quality of care you receive to your QIO at:KEPRO

1-[PHONE-194] or TTY [PHONE-257]. The QIO is the independent reviewer authorized by Medicare to review the decision to discharge you.

e You can work with the hospital to prepare for your safe discharge and arrange for services you may need after you leave the hospital. When you no longer need inpatient hospital care, your doctor or the hospital staff will inform you of your planned discharge date.

e You can speak with your doctor or other hospital staff if you have concerns about being discharged.

Your Right to Appeal Your Hospital Discharge:

* You have the right to an immediate, independent medical review (appeal) of the decision to

discharge you from the hospital. If you do this, you will not have to pay for the services you receive during the appeal (except for charges like copays and deductibles).

If you choose to appeal, the independent reviewer will ask for your opinion. The reviewer also will look at your medical records and/or other relevant information. You do not have to prepare anything in writing, but you have the right to do so if you wish.

If you choose to appeal, you and the reviewer will each receive a copy of a detailed explanation about why your covered hospital stay should not continue. You will receive this detailed notice only after you request an appeal.

If the QIO finds that you are not ready to be discharged from the hospital, Medicare will continue to cover your hospital services.

If the QIO agrees services should no longer be covered after the discharge date, neither Medicare nor your Medicare health plan will pay for your hospital stay after noon of the day

after the QIO notifies you of its decision. If you stop services no later than that time, you will avoid financial liability.

If you do not appeal, you may have to pay for any services you receive after your discharge date. See page 2 of this notice for more information. Form CMS 10065-IM (Exp. [DOB-256]) OMB approval 0938-1019

Protocol: <Rapid Response Protocol Protocol> wie Rapid Response Protocol] *** A. Nursing Orders: (All patients) Insert peripheral IV if No patent IVY access Establish and maintain the patient's airway Continuous cardiac monitoring place on bedside monitor Initiate Oxygen Therapy Protocol * Oxygen Therapy: Only start on Oxygen therapy if SpOZ is less than

than 90% * Device: Nasal Cannula * Rate: 1 Liter per minute 2 L/Min

* Initiate 02 Therapy Protocol: ‘Yes No

* Initiate 02 weaning protecol: Yes No

* Titrate to Maintain Spe: 90-96%

if greater than 51 nasal cannula required change to face mask starting at 40% Fi02 and Notify provider.

Suction Airway as needed

Notify attending physician of change in patient status and interventions performed,

Fingerstick blood glucose now

Give 25 milliliters of D50 if blood glucose below 80

Give 50 milliliters of D050 if blood glucose below 60

B. Cardiac Clinical Changes:

Heart Rate less than 40 (symptomatic)

1.) Atropine 1 milligram intravenous push now per ACLS protocol Heart Rate greater than 180 (symptomatic)

1.) 12 Lead EKG Now Chest Pain 1.) EKG Now and give to a provider within 10 minutes - may give to ED provider or in-house provider.

2.) Aspirin 81 milligrams orally x 4 chewed and swallow if no allergies, active bleeding, warfarin use, or unless taken within

the last 24 hours 3.) Nitroglycerin 0.4 milligrams sublingual, may repeat every 5 minutes x2 doses if systolic BP greater than 90

4.) Troponin stat 5.) Upon identification of ST-Elevation initiate the STEMI process. Call hospital operator to page out Stemi Alert.

Systolic Blood Pressure less than 90 (symptomatic)

1.) Normal saline 250 milliliters intravenous bolus if no crackles. rhonchi or complaints of dyspnea; may repeat x 1

C. Respiratory Allergy and Anaphylaxis:

STAT Portable Chest x-ray (obtain if an acute respiratory distress problem). Administer nebulized Albuterol 2.5 mg (unless patient is presently on a nebulizer treatment protocol) in 3 mL saline.

Arterial Blood Gas per Respiratory Therapy if unable to improve saturation with oxygen therapy and or suspected COZ retention.

If BiPap required, Initiate with the following settings. inspiratory pressure of 12 cm H20, expiratory pressure of 6cm H20, titrating as indicated Patient assessment of crackles/rhonchi and patient complaint of dyspnea 1.) administer furosemide (Lasix) 20 milligrams intravenous now. 2.) Decrease/Discontinue IV fluids

D. Respiratory (Upper Airway): altered level of consciousness, edema of or the face. lips. tongue or throat, nasal congestion, rhinitis, sneezing cough, hoarseness or quiet voice, lost ability to speak or

a sensation of tightness in the throat, strider, hypoxia:

K. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post narcotic administration:

Naloxone (Narcan) 0.2 milligrams IV push now if recent narcotic administered and any of the following are present:

1.) Decreased level of consciousness

2.) Pinpoint pupils (less than 3 mm)

3.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min

L. Altered Level of consciousness or change in mental status post benzodiazepine administration: Flumazeni] (Romazicon) 0.2 milligrams intravenous push now if recent Benzodiazepine administered and any of the following are present:

1.) Decreased level of consciousness

2.) Respiratory rate less than 8/min

Protocol: <Oxygen Therapy Protocol> -- Oxygen Therapy Protocol: Adult --

INITIATION:

A. Supplemental oxygen will occur after verification of a provider’s order. starting at the rate specified in the order.

a. The oxygen liter flow will be adjusted in 1-liter increments in order to achieve and maintain specific oxygen saturation (Sp02) target

range specified in provider order.

B. Patients will be placed on oxygen to maintain an oxygen saturation (Sp02) target range.

a. Exception: COPD patients. keep Sp02 between 88-92% (unless otherwise ordered) b. Exception: Acute stroke patients, keep Sp02 greater than 94% (unless otherwise ordered) C. A nasal cannula is indicated unless unable to maintain the ordered Sp02 target range Liter flow not to exceed 6 liters/minute (LPM) 2. Assess patient need for continuous pulse oximetry when receiving greater than or equal 5 LPM 02 per nasal cannula or Fi02 greater chan 40% D. If the patient's Sp02 goal cannot be achieved with the use of a nasal cannula, the respiratory therapist (RT) should be notified and the RT may step a patient up to the next oxygen delivery device titrated to the owest level of oxygen needed to maintain target Sp02 range. Notify provider with each device change. If unable to maintain target Sp02, notify provider immediately for orders, Call Rapid Response if provider not immediately available.

. Simple mask

. Yenturid mask

. OxyMask

. Partial/non-rebreathing mask

High flow oxygen

ONITORING:

A. Adult patients included in the oxygen therapy protocol will receive oxygen saturation assessments and titration, if indicated. per guidelines for modification of oxygen therapy. RT to assess and escalate therapy as indicated.

B. If patient is in distress, contact physician immediately and do not leave patient unattended.

C. ABG Indications:

1. If unable to obtain Sp02, a provider should be notified and an ABG a8 ordered for hemodynamic status.

f there are concerns for the patient's oxygenation or acid-base status (e.g. increase in confusion/disorientation, diaphoresis, use of accessory muscles, tachycardia, tachypnea, tachypnea, cyanosis),

a provider should be notified and an ABG ordered.

<End of Protocol>

Order Date: 12/03/22 ——Service— Category Procedure Name Order Number Date Time Pri Qty Ord Source Status Ordered By NURORDINP Oxygen Weaning Protocol 20221203-1384 12/03/22 2225 E IPR CHECHOL Other Provider : xxWILAD Sig Lv] Provider :

Protacol: <Oxygen Weaning Protocal>

~- Oxygen Weaning Protocol: Adult --

MODIFICATION GUIDELINES:

A. Notify patient's nurse of all oxygen titrations if completed by RT. B. All titrations must be appropriately documented.

C. Once patient is within ordered target Sp02 range and vital signs are stable per vital sign parameter order, proceed to weaning:

1. Simple face mask patients who require liter flow less than 6 LPM will need to be switched to a nasal cannula starting with a flow rate of less than 3 LPM. 2. For patients on blended oxygen, the Fi02 will be managed by RT in increments of 10% while maintaining the target Sp02 range from order.

3. RT to convert to nasal cannula when Fi02 is less than 40%.

4. Nasal cannula titration will begin with decrease in liter flow by 1 LPM, to lowest liter flow needed to maintain target Sp02 range.

5. If tolerated, continue to wean oxygen to room air, using discontinuation guidelines.

a. Oxygen therapy should not be discontinued/weaned for patients with

a documented history of chronic hypoxemia (e.g. COPD) that wear

oxygen at home unless otherwise ordered by physician.

D. If patient unable to maintain target Sp02, discontinue weaning and follow Oxygen Therapy Protocol. Maintain the lowest Fi02/liter flow required to keep Sp02 at target range.

E. Notify physician if patient is not able to wean for home 02 evaluation order.

DISCONTINUATION GUIDELINES:

A. Once patient is on 1 LPM or less, place on room air.

1. Check patient's Sp02 within 1 hour of placing on room air and then per vital sign order unless otherwise indicated, with proper documentation.

2. Communicate discontinuation of 02 therapy to appropriate healthcare professionals.

B. If Sp02 less than ordered target range, resume 02 therapy and follow Oxygen Therapy Protocol.

<End of Protocol>

FEED PATIENT: MARSHALL, DEBBIE A/S: 66 F ADMIT: 12/03/22 ACCOUNT NO: G00631985908 LOC: G.ERHOLD DISCH/DEP: 12/04/22 RM: G.ERII STATUS: IN ATTEND DR: Chen.Chun-Cheng MD BD: A UNIT NO: G001075275 REPORT STATUS: FINAL Protocol: <MRSA Screen/Targeted Decol.3 Protocol> MRSA Screening and Targeted Decolonization Protocol SCREENING:

- Obtain MRSA nares screening swab on ALL admissions for the following criteria, if none of the listed criteria is met Nursing may cancel the swab order:

1. Prior MRSA history in Meditech - located within First Point of Contact screen or Health History

Active MRSA less than 1 year with positive culture and/or active infection: Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

If known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures: Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS

2. First Point of Contact NUR inpatient admission/transfer queries for high risk:

Nursing home

Long term care facility

Other healthcare facility

Other hospital

Jail/prison

Homeless shelter

End stage renal dialysis care

Surgical procedure: Open heart, spine, or joint replacement

Known IY Drug User and/or draining wounds

3. Nasal swab should be taken from anterior nares, not deep

-If applicable, primary site (e.g. wound) should also be swabbed

4. Only swab patient's nares who have been off anti-MRSA antibiotics for at least 48 hours

DECOLONIZATION:

- Target ced decolonization for NON-ICU if MRSA nares screening swab js POSITIVE, prior history of MRSA within 1 year OR patient is identified as high risk based on first point of contact screening.

- Universal decolonization for ALL adult and pediatric ICU patients

1. Implement appropriate isolation precautions when MRSA positive for prior history or current colonization or infection as follows:

Active MRSA Tess than 1 year with positive culture and/or active infection : Implement CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

History of MRSA less than 1 year with no active drainage or other signs of infection: Implement MODIFIED CONTACT PRECAUTIONS

Tf known MRSA carrier greater than 1 year with no positive cultures: Follow STANDARD PRECAUTIONS 2. Concurrently begin: Daily chlorhexidine (CHG) bathing for 5 consecutive days or longer if patient has central venous access device or in ICU

upirocin or jlodophor to nares twice daily for 5 consecutive days

3. Decolonization criteria:

All patients in Intensive care unit, patients identified as high

risk on the first point of contact screen, patients known to be

RSA positive by prior history or new positive lab results

ise an alternative for patients with known allergy to mupirocin or jodine

Continue mupirecin/iodophor nasal product and CHG treatment if transferred to another level of care to complete 5 full consecutive days

Apply product to anterior nares for 30 seconds each side (slowly clockwise for count of 5, counter clockwise for count of 5)

DISCONTINUE CONTACT PRECAUTIONS FOR MRSA: - After off all anti-MRSA antibiotics and completing the decolonization protocol for 5 full consecutive days:

Protocol: <Urinary Management Protocol Protocol> ~-- URINARY MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL --- The Urinary Management Protocol is intended to fully empower nursing to utilize all resources available to them to collect accurate output, with an initial focus on using non-invasive urinary management methods. If followed correctly, this should lead to significant reduction in indwelling urinary catheter (TUC) use.

NOTE: This protocol does not apply to patients who have had urological surgery, indwelling urinary catheters placed by urology. or have a urology consult.

PRE-CATHETER AVOIDANCE REVIEW AND EXCLUSION (P-CARE)

On admission. evaluate ability to capture urinary output using the processes below.

- If TUC is ordered, complete 2-person attestation w/ approval prior to insertion

* TUCs can be approved up to first 48 hours then reviewed daily for:

“ Critical 180 requiring hourly reads

“ CBI w/ active hematuria

“GU surgery

“ Proning > 12 hours on paralytics

“ Sedated AND paralyzed

“If chronic IUC vetted and ordered, keep in place

“Urology ordered: Need active plan of care and oversight while

patient inhouse ~ FOR PATIENTS WITH ACUTE RETENTION: * Perform bladder scan:

“ If residual urine >/= 500 mL:

Drain bladder via in/out catheter Follow UCARE (see below)

“ If residual urine < 500 mL:

Deplay active voiding (if tolerated): * Ambulate patient to toilet /BSC

* Stand to void * Raise HOB, bend knees (urine pose) * Run nands in warm water * Gently massage over bladde * Consider medications (e.g. BPH/alpha blocker)

* Assess/consider other causative factors, such as contributing

meds (e.g. opioids, antihistamines, anticholinergics)

- FOR PATIENTS WITH ACUTE KIDNEY INJURY (AKT) OR END-STAGE RENAL DISEASE (ESRD) OR KIDNEY DISEASE REQUIRING RENAL REPLACEMENT THERAPY (RRT):

* For patients with ESRD: “~ Discontinue IUC after consulting provider * For patients with AKI: “If urinary output >/= 15 mL/or for > 48 hours: Discontinue IUC after consulting provider

“ If urinary output < 15 mL/hr for » 48 hours: Perform bladder scan every 6 hours

* Tf residual urine >/= 500 mL:

“Drain bladder via in/out catheter

NURSE-DRIVEN FOLEY PROTOCOL (NDFP)

NDFP empowers nursing to remove indwelling urinary catheters (IUC) as soon as they are no longer clinically indicated. Nurses can remove the urinary catheter without a specific order or provider approval.

A. Appropriate indications for maintaining an indwelling urinary catheter include:

1. Accurate 180 and critically 171]

2. Acute retention/obstruction

3. Assist in skin healing

Protocol: <Telemetry Removal NDP Protocol> -- Telemetry Nurse Driven Removal Protocol --

Telemetry with nurse driven removal protocol - telemetry can be discontinued without an additional MD order if patient no longer meets criteria for protocol.

TELEMETRY MONITORING INDICATED:

1. Significant arrhythmia requiring medical therapy: SYT (supraventricular tachycardia), bradycardia, A. Fib (atrial fibrillation) with RVR (rapid ventricular response)

2. Acute coronary syndrome or unstable angina with NSTEMI (non-ST elevation myocardial infarction) or STEMI (ST-elevation myocardial infarction)

3. Pre or post PCI (percutaneous cardiac intervention), CABG (coronary artery bypass with graft), EP (electrophysiology) study, pacemaker or AICD (automatic internal cardiac defibrillator) implantation

4. Medical/surgical patients on IV beta blockers, IV digoxin, ionotropic drips, or other medications requiring close cardiac monitoring (does not include obstetrical patients)

5. Moderate to severe hypokalemia (less than or equal to 3.0) or severe hypomagnesemia (less than or equal to 1.3)

6. Drug or chemical toxicity

7. Suspected pacemaker or AICD malfunction

8. Resuscitated from cardiac arrest or unstable VT (ventricular tachycardia)

9. Syncope of unknown etiology

10. Stroke patients

ll. Post vascular procedure

12. Acute decompensated heart failure

13. Sepsis

TELEMETRY NOT INDICATED FOR:

1. Patients who are stable and arrhythmia free for 48 hours of consecutive monitoring and does not meet any criteria in the ‘Telemetry Monitoring Indicated’ list 2. Terminally 111 and not a candidate for therapy for arrhythmia medications, comfort care patients

3. Patients with chronic, rate controlled, stable A. Fib

4. Patients with asymptomatic PVCs (premature ventricular contractions) not hospitalized for cardiac reasons

<End of Protocol>

Clinical Note Note:

66-year-old female with past medical history significant for thyroid disorder s/p moped accident earlier this evening. Fell off of moped and did hit her head. Denies LOC. Reports headache. Denies radicular pain, paresthesias, balance difficulty, nausea, vomiting. Neurosurgery consulted after CT head demonstrated acute subdural hematoma.

-Chart reviewed. Discussed with Dr. Lockney and ER provider, Per ER report, patient neuro intact. GCS 15.

-All available imaging personally reviewed and interpreted by myself and Dr. Lockney. -CT head on 12/03 demonstrates 3 mm posterior interhemispheric acute SDH

- cervical CT demonstrates no fracture or malalignment

- no acute surgical intervention

- admitted to Trauma

- qi neuro checks overnight

- SBP 90-160

- Keppra 500mg BID x 7 days

-HOB > 30 degrees

- hold all anticoagulants/antiplatelet medications

- Repeat CT head in AM or with any decline in neuro status

Please call with any questions, concerns, or change in the patient's neurological status. Mitchell Haines, DPT, PA-C Neurosurgery
